<div id="review_1621509940" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1621509940" />
    <a title="MrsJoseph *grouchy*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy"><img alt="MrsJoseph *grouchy*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475772748p2/4702933.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1621509940?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MrsJoseph *grouchy*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MrsJoseph *grouchy*" href="/user/show/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy">MrsJoseph *grouchy*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=i-cant-even">i-cant-even</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=fantasy-epic">fantasy-epic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=i-am-unable-to-can">i-am-unable-to-can</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=bookclub-reads">bookclub-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=amazing-amazingness">amazing-amazingness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=i-am-a-cover-whore">i-am-a-cover-whore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=2017-reading-challenges">2017-reading-challenges</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=need-moar-now">need-moar-now</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=terrific-terrificness">terrific-terrificness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1621509940" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15669488999361675184"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://bookslifewine.com/r-the-cloud-roads/'>http://bookslifewine.com/r-the-cloud-...</a><br/><br/>I don’t have a lot of experience with Martha Wells – one short story (of the Raksura) and that’s about it. So, I had no real expectations as to how I would enjoy this book.<br/><br/>And I did. By the end of the book, I found <i>The Cloud Roads</i> very, very interesting indeed. The first 100 pages or so didn’t go as smoothly as I’d liked and I found Moon to be shy, skittish, aloof, moody and TSTL. <br/><br/>Yes. I said it. Moon behaves much in the way a TSTL Romance heroine. He had </span>
  <span id="freeText15669488999361675184" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bookslifewine.com/r-the-cloud-roads/">http://bookslifewine.com/r-the-cloud-...</a><br /><br />I don’t have a lot of experience with Martha Wells – one short story (of the Raksura) and that’s about it. So, I had no real expectations as to how I would enjoy this book.<br /><br />And I did. By the end of the book, I found <i>The Cloud Roads</i> very, very interesting indeed. The first 100 pages or so didn’t go as smoothly as I’d liked and I found Moon to be shy, skittish, aloof, moody and TSTL. <br /><br />Yes. I said it. Moon behaves much in the way a TSTL Romance heroine. He had a constant monologue running in his head “Should I stay? Should I go? Should I try? Should I not?” It’s all quite frustrating for a reader who hates TSTL heroines (and now add heroes to that list). I sympathized with Moon – he’s had a hard and lonely life. Moon’s entire family was killed, he doesn’t know <i>what</i> he is (let alone who he is) and most of the time he gets kicked out of whatever settlement he’s living in just when he feels like he’s found a place of his own. <br /><br />All of that must play havoc on the soul (and the attitude), so I gave Moon some leeway. But still...<br /><br /><em>The Cloud Roads</em> has a very slow start and build up. I was over 100 pages before I started to feel…compelled to read. Sadly, up to that point I was rather bored of it all (but determined to finish). Once I got over that slow hump, I was pretty much hooked, however. I love the way Wells switched gendered politics. I love that the Raksura are ruled by Queens and that the Consorts are... “high-strung and shy with delicate sensibilities.” <br /><br /><blockquote>"You were expecting a consort from Star Aster," he said, "a sheltered, spoiled consort with a perfect bloodline. Are you asking me to believe that it wasn't a shock when Stone showed up with me?" <br /><br />"I've known Stone all my life. I'm not surprised at anything he shows up with. You can't have come from the bad bloodline; you're strong, healthy, and your conformation is perfect." Jade lifted her brows. "And you're high-strung, shy, and have the same delicate sensibilities of every gently bred and sheltered consort I've ever met." <br />-page 167</blockquote><br /><br />I think the biggest issue I had with <em>The Cloud Roads</em> is...the lack of emotion and relationship building. I didn’t really see Moon develop a relationship with Jade or almost anyone besides Stone and Chime (and maybe Flower). So it was difficult to understand why Jade was so interested in him (outside of him being the only consort around, that is).<br /><br />As much as I think Moon is a bit TSTL, he has an incredibly generous soul. He wants to help people and would probably give up the shirt on his back to someone in need. He's the type of guy you want in your corner when the shit hits the fan. <s>Even</s> <em>Especially</em> in a crisis, Moon has your back. Even though he felt like an unwanted outsider, Moon was ready and willing to fight on behalf of Indigo Cloud with no questions asked. Loved that about Moon. <br /><br />I did like the other members of Indigo Cloud – what little I got to know of them, that is. Most of the characters are lightly sketched in but this does NOT feel like the characters are poorly done, more like the reader is limited to what Moon knows and Moon is shy and moody.<br /><br />I never truly understood or liked Pearl and I hated the way she treated Moon. I still am not sure why she was so nasty to him to begin with – jealously doesn’t seem to apply.<br /><br /><blockquote>Moon was terrified of not fitting into the court, so afraid that he was willing to let Pearl force him out, when instinct said to fight to stay. <br />-page 175</blockquote><br /><br />By the end of <em>The Cloud Roads</em>, I firmly believed that Moon is TSTL (OMG, I wanted to choke him at the end when he pulled one of my most hated TSTL heroine moves. Slowly. Choke.) but I wanted to just hug his stupid neck. I was also totally in love with the kiddies and starting to warm up to Jade (who has my favorite quote in the book). <br /><blockquote><br />[Redacted] grinned at Jade, her jaw distended to show a startling array of teeth. "Come now, we're kin. We should be friends." <br /><br />Jade grinned back. "I'm going to rip your womb out and eat it." Then she launched herself at [redacted]’s throat.<br />-page 256</blockquote><br /><br />I [still have] a few questions: I'm not quite sure about the Abrora - do they shift (as well) but without wings? And if they are fertile, why are they bothered about queens and consorts? And can only consorts mate with queens or is it that only consorts and queens make royal clutches?<br /><br />Even with those questions, I totally plan to finish up this series. The world building is fascinating; the characters are layered and I enjoyed the writing (once Wells decided to get moving). I do recommend this book with the caution that it will be a slow start.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15669488999361675184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bwj5rGlHWSZQFUz2oJrMd8G6i2qe59IT+pNN4SWacFXWtPZoPK3TbBiYJNevQTXtP+orC2HrkIJh4rRrXqBjRw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EHmEhZrrsfR2rohrcTFWGbhNAtvlonTWUvyaN5h/WgepxYtBzwE7vj4j4Ep+6q+DRh2iuhquNkfJjWO940VJFQ==')})
  }

          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3265480979141169683"> Martha Wells has written many fantasy novels, including The Books of the Raksura series (beginning with <i>The Cloud Roads</i>), the Ile-Rien series (including <i>The Death of the Necromancer</i>) as well as YA fantasy novels, short stories, media tie-ins (for <i>Star Wars</i> and <i>Stargate: Atlantis</i>), and non-fiction. Her most recent fantasy novel is <i>The Harbors of the Sun</i> in 2017, the final novel in The Books of the</span>
  <span id="freeText3265480979141169683" style="display:none"> Martha Wells has written many fantasy novels, including The Books of the Raksura series (beginning with <i>The Cloud Roads</i>), the Ile-Rien series (including <i>The Death of the Necromancer</i>) as well as YA fantasy novels, short stories, media tie-ins (for <i>Star Wars</i> and <i>Stargate: Atlantis</i>), and non-fiction. Her most recent fantasy novel is <i>The Harbors of the Sun</i> in 2017, the final novel in The Books of the Raksura series. She has a new series of SF novellas, <i>The Murderbot Diaries</i>, published by Tor.com in 2017 and 2018. She was also the lead writer for the story team of <i>Magic: the Gathering</i>'s Dominaria expansion in 2018. She has won a Nebula Award, two Hugo Awards, an ALA/YALSA Alex Award, a Locus Award, and her work has appeared on the Philip K. Dick Award ballot, the USA Today Bestseller List, and the New York Times Bestseller List. Her books have been published in eleven languages. <br /><br />She has had short stories in the magazines <i>Black Gate</i>, <i>Realms of Fantasy</i>, <i>Lone Star Stories</i>, <i>Lightspeed Magazine</i>, and <i>Stargate Magazine</i>, and in the Tsunami Relief anthology <i>Elemental</i>, <i>The Other Half of the Sky</i>, <i>Tales of the Emerald Serpent</i>, <i>Mech: Age of Steel</i>, and <i>The Gods of Lovecraft</i>. <br /><br />She has essays in the nonfiction anthologies <i>Farscape Forever</i>, <i>Mapping the World of Harry Potter</i>, <i>Chicks Unravel Time</i>, and <i>The Kobold Guide to Magic</i>. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3265480979141169683" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
